Taharah — Purification
intermediate
12 min
Istihalah: Transformation as a Means of Purification
Explains istihalah as a purifier with proof and intra-Hanafi dispute on ash.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle that complete transformation (istihalah) purifies impure substances, apply it to cases like ash and soap, and identify the intra-Hanafi disagreement on ash purity.

Core Idea
When a substance completely transforms, its impurity ruling is lifted — istihalah is a purifier.

In Hanafi fiqh, purification extends beyond washing. One key principle is istihalah: the complete transformation of an impure substance into something new. This lesson examines the evidence from the analogy of the embryo and the wine-vinegar process, and explores applications like burnt dung, soap, and vinegar. You will also encounter a classical intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani regarding ash.

Guided Path
1
Identify the principle
What is istihalah and how does it bring about purification? List the examples given: wine to vinegar, dead animal to salt, dung to ash.
Istihalah is a change in the very substance (inqilab al-'ayn).
2
Trace the proof
How does the analogy of nutfah-alaqah-mudghah and juice-wine-vinegar establish that transformation removes impurity? Identify the common illa.
The illa is complete transformation of the substance.
3
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad differ on ash from burnt dung. State each position and the basis. Abu Yusuf says impurity remains; Muhammad says it becomes pure.
Abu Hanifa sided with Muhammad per al-Muhit.
4
Resolve the mudghah contradiction
An apparent contradiction arises: mudghah is said to be pure in the analogy but impure elsewhere. How is it resolved? Distinguish between makhluqah (ensouled) and ghayr makhluqah (not ensouled).
Only the mudghah without soul is impure; with soul, it is pure.
5
Apply to modern cases
Apply the principle to soap made from impure oil and to a mouse falling into juice that transforms into vinegar. What is the ruling?
Fatwa relies on Muhammad's view for soap; for ash, some later fatwa follow Abu Yusuf.

فظهر بهذا أن المطهرات عشرة كما ذكره في المجتبى ناقلا عن صلاة الجلابي.
Then know that it has become apparent up to here that purification is achieved by four things: washing, rubbing, drying, and wiping on polished surfaces without water, and rubbing is included in rubbing, and the fifth is wiping cupping glasses with water and cloth as we mentioned. And the sixth is fire, as we mentioned regarding earth when it is burned by fire. And the seventh is transformation of the substance: if it is in wine, there is no disagreement on purification; if it is in other substances like a pig or dead animal falling into a salt pit and becoming edible salt, and dung and feces burning and becoming ash, it becomes purified according to Muhammad, contrary to Abu Yusuf, and Abu Hanifa is joined to Muhammad in al-Muhit, and many mashayikh chose Muhammad's view. And in al-Khulasa: the fatwa is upon it, and in Fath al-Qadir it is the chosen view because the Law established the description of impurity on that reality, and the reality is negated by negation of some parts of its concept, so how about all of it? For salt is not bone and flesh, so when it becomes salt, the ruling of salt applies. Its analogy in the law is that the nutfah is impure, becomes an alaqah which is impure, becomes a mudghah which becomes pure; and juice is pure, becomes wine and becomes impure, becomes vinegar and becomes pure. Thus we know that transformation of the substance entails removal of the description attached to it. He said: (except) for mani, i.e., except for cupping glasses and the place of phlebotomy, for wiping there is like washing as passed. He said: and its analogy in the law of nutfah etc. is contrary to the issue of rubbing mani, so reflect. Then I saw some virtuous person mention the following text: There is consideration because we have stated that the alaqah and mudghah are impure like mani, and this is explicitly stated in al-Nihayah and al-Tabyin, and that was mentioned in al-Bahr. And it is astonishing that al-Bahr author ruled there that mudghah is impure and here he narrates from al-Fath that it is pure, and he accepted it and was followed by the author of al-Minh in both places without commenting, and no one hides the contradiction in that. And the apparent is that it is impure due to the explicit statement of al-Nihayah and al-Tabyin, and due to what preceded in al-Nifas from al-Khulasa that the miscarriage if nothing of its creation is apparent is like blood. So the apparent from 'non-apparent creation' is that it is a mudghah not fully formed, and its ruling is like blood, meaning it has not left the reality of blood like nutfah and alaqah, both of which are impure, so the mudghah is impure, so deliberate. Then it occurred to me that the contradiction can be resolved by interpreting the ruling of impurity to apply to the mudghah not fully formed, i.e., that into which the spirit has not been breathed, and the ruling of purity to apply to the mudghah fully formed, i.e., that into which the spirit has been breathed. We narrated in al-Nifas from the exegetes that they said concerning the verse [Surah al-Hajj: 5] that takhliq is by breathing the spirit. So the fully formed is that into which the spirit is breathed, and the non-fully formed is that into which the spirit is not breathed. According to this, it should be considered that breathing the spirit is one of the purifiers, as is not hidden, and Allah knows best. Soap made from impure oil. And in al-Mujtaba: Using impure fat in soap, fatwa is given on its purification because it has changed, and change purifies according to Muhammad, and fatwa is given for need. And in al-Zahiriyyah: Ash of dung is pure according to Abu Yusuf, contrary to Muhammad, and the fatwa is on Abu Yusuf's view, which is the opposite of the transmitted ikhtilaf, for it implies that ash is pure according to Muhammad, impure according to Abu Yusuf, as is not hidden. And in it also: Feces if buried in a place until they become dust, it is said they become pure, like a dead donkey falling into a salt pit and becoming salt, which is purified according to Muhammad. And in al-Khulasa: A mouse fell into a jar of wine and it became vinegar, it is purified by the mouse before becoming vinegar; if the mouse disintegrates in it, it is not permissible. And if a mouse falls into juice, then the juice becomes wine, then becomes vinegar, it is not like the case of falling into wine; that is the chosen view. Similarly, if a dog laps from juice, then it becomes wine, then becomes vinegar, it is not purified. And in al-Zahiriyyah: If water is poured into wine, then the wine becomes vinegar, it is purified, and that is sahih. And in Fath al-Qadir, purification by fire is included in transformation, but there is no necessary connection between them, for if one removes the place of blood from a sheep's head, it becomes pure; and an oven sprayed with impure water, there is no harm in baking bread in it, as in al-Mujtaba. Similarly, impure clay if made into a jug or pot and put in fire becomes pure, as in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. And the eighth is tanning, which has passed, and the ninth is slaughtering, so every animal whose skin is purified by tanning is purified by slaughtering as we have mentioned. And the tenth is drawing water from wells as we have explained. Thus it is apparent that the purifiers are ten, as mentioned in al-Mujtaba, quoting from Salat al-Jilabi.
Source pages p. 394

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on istihalah (transformation) as a means of purification. The author lists four previously mentioned purifiers (washing, rubbing, drying, wiping on polished surfaces) and adds more: fifth, wiping cupping glasses with water and cloth; sixth, fire for earth; seventh, transformation of the substance itself. Transformation is the key topic: when an impure substance changes into a completely different substance, it becomes pure. Examples: wine turning to vinegar, a dead animal in a salt pit turning to salt, dung burning to ash. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Muhammad says ash from burnt dung becomes pure, Abu Yusuf disagrees. The author notes that Abu Hanifa is joined with Muhammad in al-Muhit, and many scholars prefer Muhammad's view; fatwa is given on it. The proof is based on the principle that impurity is attached to a specific reality; when that reality ceases to exist, the ruling ceases. The analogy (qiyas) is drawn from natural processes: nutfah (semen) is impure, becomes alaqah (clot) impure, then mudghah (embryo) which becomes pure. Similarly, juice becomes impure wine, then pure vinegar. The author then addresses an apparent contradiction: mudghah was stated as impure elsewhere. The resolution is that the impure mudghah is the pre-soul stage, while the pure mudghah is after the soul is breathed. The passage then discusses further applications: soap made from impure oil becomes pure because of transformation; ash from dung is ruled pure by Abu Yusuf in some texts, but the fatwa is on his view; a mouse falling into wine that turns to vinegar purifies the mouse if it hasn't disintegrated; similarly, water poured into wine turning to vinegar purifies it. The author concludes by listing ten purifiers: the ones mentioned plus tanning, slaughtering, and drawing water from wells.

Key Terms
استحالة (istihalah): Transformation of a substance into a different substance, e.g., wine to vinegar, dead animal to salt, dung to ash.
انقلاب العين (inqilab al-'ayn): Same as istihalah, transformation of the substance itself.
مضغة (mudghah): Embryo in the form of a lump of flesh. In this passage, distinguished as makhluqah (with soul) and ghayr makhluqah (without soul).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on soap made from impure oil?
A) It remains impure because the oil was najis.
B) It becomes pure because the oil has changed (istihalah).
C) It is makruh but permissible.
D) It depends on the type of oil.

Key Takeaway
Istihalah (complete transformation) is a recognized purifier in the Hanafi school, supported by qiyas on natural processes and applied to cases like ash, soap, and vinegar, with an intra-school variance on ash.

Taharah — Purification

Excused Amount of Thick Impurity (Ma'fu 'Anh)
Ruling on excused thick impurity with evidence and disputes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the excused amount of thick impurity in the Hanafi school, identify its proofs, and explain the intra-Hanafi disputes regarding expansion and penetration.

Core Idea
A dirham-size of thick impurity is excused in prayer; the measurement is at the moment of contact.

In the Hanafi school, not every impurity on the body or clothing invalidates prayer. This lesson establishes the threshold for thick impurities (najis mughallad) like blood, urine, or wine. We will examine the authoritative measure of a dirham (palm's width), its juristic proofs, and important nuances regarding expansion and penetration across garment layers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
The passage states that an amount of thick impurity equal to a dirham (approximately the width of the palm) is excused ('afwa) during prayer. Note that this applies only to thick impurities, not light ones (e.g., infant urine).
Other schools may have different measures.
2
Examine the evidence (dalil)
The author cites two proofs: (1) the text of istinja with stones (where the stone cleans an area of a dirham, yet the stone itself is not a purifier), and (2) consensus (ijma) that this amount is excused. Understand that the dirham measure is derived from these sources.
The stone is not a purifier, but it is used for istinja up to a dirham size, implying that amount is excusable.
3
Analyze the time of measurement
The critical moment is the time of contact (مقابل وقت الإصابة). If the impurity contacts the body or garment in a quantity less than a dirham, it is excused even if it later spreads. However, if it spreads before prayer begins, the majority holds that the excuse is lost.
Al-Marghinani and a group hold that expansion after contact does not remove the excuse; the majority disagree.
4
Understand the penetration rule
If a garment is single-layered, impurity that penetrates to the other side is considered the same impurity, not additional. For a double-layered garment (e.g., lined), penetration may create separate impurity on each layer, thus potentially exceeding the excused amount.
The text is cut off; the complete ruling distinguishes between one and two layers.
5
Apply the ruling to cases
Given the conditions, evaluate scenarios: a drop of blood of dirham size on the sleeve – valid if prayed before it spreads. If it spreads to double the size before prayer, the majority says prayer invalid. If the garment is a single thickness, penetration does not multiply the impurity.
Use the dirham measure as a practical benchmark.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (وعفى قدر الدرهم كعرض الكف من نجس مغلظ كالدم والبول والخمر وخرء الدجاج وبول ما لا يؤكل لحمه والروث والخشى لأن ما لا يأخذه الطرف كوقع الذباب مخصوص من نص التطهر اتفاقاً فيخص أيضاً قدر الدرهم بنص الاستنجاء بالحجر لأن محله قدره ولم يكن الحجر مطهراً حتى لو دخل في قليل ماء نجسه، أو بدلالة الإجماع عليه. والمعتبر وقت الإصابة فلو كان دهناً نجساً قدر درهم فانفرش فصار أكثر منه لا يمنع في اختيار المرغيناني وجماعة ومختار غيرهم المنع؛ فلو صلى قبل اتساعه جازت وبعده أخذ الأكثرون كذا في السراج الوهاج. ولا يعتبر نفوذ المقدار إلى الوجه الآخر إذا كان الثوب واحداً لأن النجاسة حينئذ واحدة في الجانبين فلا يعتبر متعدداً بخلاف ما إذا كان ذا
He said: And the amount of a dirham is excused, like the palm of the hand from thick impurity, such as blood, urine, wine, chicken droppings, and urine of what is not eaten, and dung and [؟]. Because what the tip does not take, like the landing of a fly, is excluded from the text of purification by consensus, so also the amount of a dirham is excluded by the text of istinja with a stone, because its place is that amount and the stone is not a purifier, even if it enters little water it makes it impure, or by indication of consensus upon it. And the consideration is at the time of contact; so if there was impure oil of the amount of a dirham and it spreads and becomes more than that, it does not prevent according to the choice of al-Marghinani and a group, and the choice of others is prevention; so if he prayed before its expansion, it is valid, and after, the majority took [the view of prevention]. As in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. And the penetration of the amount to the other side is not considered if the garment is one, because the impurity then is one in both sides, so it is not considered multiple, unlike if it is [two layers].
Source pages p. 395

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof on the excused amount of thick impurity (najis mughallad). The baseline is that an impurity less than the size of a dirham (approximately the palm of the hand) is excused in prayer. The evidence is: just as a tiny amount like a fly's landing is exempted by consensus, the dirham amount is also exempted by the text of istinja with stones, where the place cleaned is that amount and the stone itself is not a purifier. Also, there is consensus. The time of measurement is the moment of contact with impurity. If an impurity of a dirham's size spreads and becomes larger, there is an ikhtilaf: al-Marghinani and some say it does not prevent (i.e., still excused), but others say it does prevent. The majority view is that if one prays after expansion, it is not valid. Additionally, if a garment is single-layered, impurity penetrating to the other side is not considered separate so the ruling remains one; but if the garment has two layers (like a lining), then the penetration may be considered an additional impurity.

Key Terms
قدر الدرهم (qadr al-dirham): The size of a silver dirham coin, approximately the width of the palm. Used as the standard for excused amounts of thick impurity.
كعرض الكف (ka 'ard al-kaff): Like the width of the palm, used to approximate the size of a dirham.
نجس مغلظ (najis mughallad): Thick (heavy) impurity, such as blood, urine, wine, feces of non-edible animals, etc.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the excused amount of thick impurity (najis mughallad) on the body or clothes during prayer?
A) Any amount is excused.
B) The size of a dirham (palm's width).
C) The size of a fingertip.
D) Only if it cannot be seen.

Key Takeaway
A dirham-sized amount of thick impurity is excused in prayer; the measurement is at the moment of contact, and expansion before prayer is a disputed but majority-rejected excuse.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
8 min
The Dirham Ruling: Excused Amount of Impurity in Prayer
Lists examples and conditions of the excused dirham-sized impurity in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the excused amount of najasah in prayer (dirham) and apply its conditions regarding spreading, layering, and carrying impure objects.

Core Idea
A dirham-sized impurity is excused in prayer, but spreading or doubling through layers removes the concession.

In this passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, the author explains the Hanafi position on the amount of impurity that is pardoned during prayer. The school holds that a heavy impurity (mughallaz) up to the size of a dirham (approximately the width of the palm) does not invalidate prayer, though it is disliked (makruh tahrimi). The ruling is derived from the practice of istinja' with stones, where a dirham-sized area is the maximum. However, this concession is subject to conditions: the impurity must not have spread before prayer, must not penetrate both sides of a double-layered garment, and must not be carried by the worshipper in a way that attributes it to him.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is praying while carrying a najasah of a dirham's amount. The ruling is that the prayer is valid (sahih) but disliked (makruh tahrimi) if one intentionally prays with it without removing it.
2
Analyze the condition of time and spreading
The key condition is that the impurity must be within dirham size at the moment it afflicts the garment. If it later spreads or is spread before prayer, the concession is lost. Al-Marghinani and a group hold that spreading after affliction does not prevent, but the majority (and the mufta bihi) say it does.
Intra-Hanafi difference
3
Examine the two-layer garment issue
If the garment has two layers, the impurity is considered multiple only if it penetrates to the other side. If it remains on one side, it is still a single dirham. Penetration means the same impurity passes through, not just contact.
4
Understand attribution when carrying impure objects
If a worshipper carries something impure that does not support itself (like a child who cannot stand), the impurity is attributed to him and invalidates the excused amount. If the object supports itself (e.g., a child sitting on his lap), the impurity is not attributed and the prayer is valid.
5
Apply the ruling to practical scenarios
Using the conditions above, determine the validity of prayer in cases like a pigeon on the head, a corpse, or discovering impurity during prayer. The guidance on whether to break prayer depends on available time and congregation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كعرض الكف من نجس مغلظ كالدم والبول والخمر وخرء الدجاج وبول ما لا يؤكل لحمه والروث والخشى لأن ما لا يأخذه الطرف كوقع الذباب مخصوص من نص التطهر اتفاقاً فيخص أيضاً قدر الدرهم بنص الاستنجاء بالحجر لأن محله قدره ولم يكن الحجر مطهراً حتى لو دخل في قليل ماء نجسه، أو بدلالة الإجماع عليه. والمعتبر وقت الإصابة فلو كان دهناً نجساً قدر درهم فانفرش فصار أكثر منه لا يمنع في اختيار المرغيناني وجماعة ومختار غيرهم المنع ؛ فلو صلى قبل اتساعه جازت وبعده أخذ الأكثرون كذا في السراج الوهاج. ولا يعتبر نفوذ المقدار إلى الوجه الآخر إذا كان الثوب واحداً لأن النجاسة حينئذ واحدة في الجانبين فلا يعتبر متعدداً بخلاف ما إذا كان ذا طاقين لتعددها يصح هذا فيمنع، وعن فرع المنع لو صلى مع درهم متنجس الوجهين لوجود الفاصل بين وجهه وهو جواهر سمكه، ولأنه مما لا ينفذ نفس ما في أحد الوجهين فيه فلم تكن النجاسة متحدة فيهما. ثم إنما يعتبر المانع مضافاً إليه، فلو جلس الصبي المتنجس الثوب والبدن في حجر المصلي وهو يستمسك أو الحمام المتنجس على رأسه جازت صلاته لأنه الذي يستعمله فلم يكن حامل النجاسة بخلاف ما لو حمل من لا يستمسك حيث يصير مضافاً إليه فلا يجوز. كذا في فتح القدير. ولو حمل ميتاً إن كان كافراً لا مطلقاً، وإن كان مسلماً لم يغسل فكذلك وإن غسل فإن استهل صحت وإلا فلا ومراده من العفو صحة الصلاة بدون إزالته لا عدم الكراهة لما في السراج الوهاج وغيره إن كانت النجاسة قدر الدرهم تكره الصلاة معها إجماعاً وإن كانت أقل وقد دخل في الصلاة نظر إن كان في الوقت سعة فالأفضل إزالتها واستقبال الصلاة وإن كانت تفوته الجماعة فإن كان يجد الماء ويجد جماعة آخرين في موضع آخر فكذلك أيضاً ليكون مؤدياً للصلاة الجائزة بيقين، وإن كان في آخر الوقت أو لا يدرك الجماعة في موضع آخر يمضي على صلاته ولا يقطعها اهـ. والظاهر أن الكراهة تحريمية لتجويزهم رفض الصلاة لأجلها ولا ترفض لأجل المكروه تنزيهاً، وسوى في فتح القدير بين الدرهم وما دونه في الكراهة ورفض الصلاة وكذا في النهاية والمحيط. وفي الخلاصة ما يقتضي الفرق بينهما فإنه قال : وقدر الدرهم لا يمنع ويكون مسيئاً أو إن كان أقل فالأفضل أن يغسلها ولا يكون مسيئاً .اهـ. وأراد بالدرهم المثقال الذي وزنه عشرون قيراطاً. وعن شمس الأئمة أنه يعتبر في كل زمان در همه والأول هو الصحيح. كذا في السراج الوهاج. وأفاد بقوله كعرض الكف أن المعتبر بسط الدرهم من حيث المساحة وهو قدر وصححه في الهداية وغيرها . أو قيل من حيث الوزن. والمصنف في كافيه . عرض الكف . هو قوله : (ومراده الخ) أي المصنف قوله : (والظاهر أن الكراهة تحريمية الخ) أقول : إن كان مراده الكراهة في قدر الدرهم فهو مسلم ولكن لا لما ذكره من التعليل بل لإطلاقه لها كما. الأغلب حيث تنصر رف إلى التحريمية، وإن كان مراده الكراهة مطلقاً أي فإن كانت أقل فممنوع بالنظر إلى الثاني بل الكراهة فيه تنزيهية لقوله فالأفضل إزالتها لأنه يقتضي أن عدم الإزالة فضيل ولا فضيلة في المكروه تحريماً، ولذا قال في النهر : هذا مسلم في الدرهم لا فيما دونه فعبارة السراج حينئذ كعبارة الخلاصة. وفي شرح المنية : إذا كانت أقل من قدر الدرهم يستحب غسلها وإن كانت قدر الدرهم يجب، وإن زاد يفرض اهـ. وذكر بعض الفضلاء عن ابن أمير حاج وفي الخانية وغيرها : إذا شرع في الصلاة فرأى في ثوبه نجاسة أقل من قدر الدرهم إن كان مقتدياً وعلم أنه لو قطع الصلاة وغسل النجاسة يدرك إمامه في الصلاة أو يدرك جماعة أخرى في موضع آخر فإنه يقطع الصلاة ويغسل الثوب لأنه قطع للإكمال، وإن كان في آخر الوقت أو لا يدرك جماعة أخرى فلا اهـ. وغير خاف أن
Like the width of the palm from heavy impurity such as blood, urine, wine, chicken droppings, urine of what is not eaten, dung, and dry dung. Because what the finger does not pick up, like the landing of a fly, is excluded from the text of purification by consensus, so also the amount of a dirham is specified by the text of purification with a stone because its place is its amount, and the stone is not a purifier such that if it entered a little water it would make it najis, or by the evidence of consensus upon it. And the consideration is at the time of affliction. So if there was oily najis of a dirham's amount and it spread and became more than that, it does not prevent (the validity of prayer) according to the choice of al-Marghinani and a group, and the choice of others is that it does prevent. So if he prayed before its expansion, it is permissible, and after it, the majority hold [the prevention]. As in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. And penetration of the amount to the other side is not considered if the garment is single-layered because then the najasah is one in both sides, so it is not considered multiple. Contrary to if it has two layers, due to multiplicity, this is correct, and it prevents. And from the branch of prevention: if he prayed with a dirham that is najis on both sides, due to the presence of a barrier between its two sides, which is the substance of its thickness, and because the essence in one side does not penetrate into it, so the najasah is not unified in them. Then, the preventive is considered as added to him. So if an impure child (whose clothes and body are najis) sits in the lap of the praying person while he is holding himself, or an impure pigeon on his head, his prayer is permissible because he is the one using it, so he is not a carrier of najasah. Contrary to if he carries someone who does not hold himself, where it becomes added to him and thus not permissible. As in Fath al-Qadir. And if he carries a corpse: if it is a disbeliever, unconditionally not [allowed]; if it is a Muslim not washed, likewise; if washed, then if the baby took a breath (i.e., was born alive), it is valid, otherwise not. And his intent by 'pardoning' is the validity of prayer without removing it, not the absence of dislike, because in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj and others: if the najasah is the amount of a dirham, prayer with it is disliked by consensus. And if it is less, and he has entered prayer, consideration: if there is ample time, it is best to remove it and restart prayer. And if he will miss the congregation, if he finds water and finds another congregation in another place, then likewise, to perform the prayer that is certainly valid. And if at the end of time or cannot catch another congregation, he continues his prayer and does not break it. End. And it appears that the dislike is prohibitional because they permit abandoning prayer for it, and one does not abandon prayer for something dislike-de-tanzih. And in Fath al-Qadir, he equated between the dirham and less than it in dislike and abandoning prayer, and likewise in al-Nihaya and al-Muhit. And in al-Khulasa, there is an indication of difference between them, for it said: 'The amount of a dirham does not prevent and he is a wrongdoer; or if it is less, it is best to wash it and he is not a wrongdoer.' End. And by 'dirham' he means the mithqal which weighs twenty qirats. And from Shams al-A'imma that in every time its dirham is considered, and the first is correct. As in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. And he indicated by his saying 'like the width of the palm' that what is considered is the spreading of the dirham in terms of area, and it is the amount, as corrected in al-Hidaya and others. Or it is said by weight. And the author in his Kafi: 'the width of the palm' is that. His statement: (And his intent etc.) i.e., the author. His statement: (And it appears that the dislike is prohibitional etc.) I say: If he intends dislike for the amount of a dirham, it is acknowledged but not due to the reason he mentioned, rather due to the absolute usage; for most cases, when [the text is] absolute, it is turned to prohibitional. If he intends dislike absolutely, i.e., even if less, then it is prevented with respect to the second, rather the dislike is tanzihi because of his saying 'it is best to remove it', as it implies that non-removal is virtuous, and there is no virtue in a prohibitional disliked thing. Hence al-Nahr said: 'This is acknowledged for the dirham, not for less than it.' So the expression of al-Siraj is like that of al-Khulasa. And in Sharh al-Munya: 'If it is less than a dirham, it is recommended to wash it; if it is a dirham, it is obligatory; if more, it is obligatory (or even fard).' End. And some virtuous people mentioned from Ibn Amir Haj and in al-Khaniyya and others: If one starts prayer and sees in his garment najasah less than a dirham, if he is a follower and knows that if he cuts the prayer and washes the najasah he will catch up with his imam in the prayer or catch another congregation in another place, then he cuts the prayer and washes the garment because it is cutting for completion; if at the end of time or he cannot catch another congregation, then he does not cut. End. And it is not hidden that...
Source pages p. 395

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a commentary on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq regarding the excused amount of najasah in prayer. The author explains that heavy impurities (mughallaz) such as blood, urine, wine, etc., are excused if they are the size of a dirham (approximately the width of the palm). This is derived from the allowance in istinja' with stones, where a dirham-sized area is the maximum. The ruling is that such an amount does not invalidate prayer, but it is disliked (makruh) with a prohibitional dislike (tahrimi) if one intentionally prays with it. The condition is that the impurity must not spread to a larger area during prayer; if it spreads before prayer, it is not excused. Also, if the garment has two layers, the impurity must not penetrate to both sides; if it does, it counts as double the amount and is no longer excused. The text includes differences of opinion within the Hanafi school: al-Marghinani and others hold that spreading after affliction but before prayer prevents validity, while others permit if the spreading occurred after the initial contact. A key point is that the excused amount is based on area (spread) not weight. Additionally, the ruling about carrying a child or animal with impurity is discussed: if the carrier is using them (like a child sitting in lap), the impurity is not attributed to the worshipper, but if he carries something that cannot hold itself, it is attributed and prevents validity. The passage ends with a discussion on whether to break prayer if one discovers minor impurity during prayer, with guidance based on time and ability to join congregation.

Key Terms
الاستحالة (al-istihalah): Transformation: the change of a najis substance into a different, pure substance, such as wine becoming vinegar, or impure oil becoming soap.
المطهرات (al-mutahhirat): Purifiers: the ten things that can purify an impure substance, including water, earth, sun, fire, transformation (istihalah), tanning, slaughter, etc.
الدباغ (al-dibagh): Tanning: a process that purifies the skin of an animal that is not eaten.
الدرهم (al-dirham): A silver coin used as a measure: in Hanafi fiqh, the excused amount of impurity is equivalent to the area of a dirham (approx. width of palm).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following correctly describes the condition for a dirham-sized impurity to be excused in a double-layered garment?
A) The impurity is excused only if it penetrates to the other side.
B) The impurity is excused if it remains on one side and does not penetrate.
C) The impurity is excused regardless of penetration because the dirham measure applies to each layer separately.
D) The impurity is not excused in double-layered garments at all.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school grants a concession for a dirham-sized heavy impurity in prayer, but this concession is tightly conditioned: the impurity must not spread before prayer, must not penetrate both sides of a double-layered garment, and must not be attributed to the worshipper through carrying an unstable impure object.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
8 min
The Excused Amount of Heavy Impurity and Its Conditions
Explains the dirham-sized excused amount of heavy impurity and its legal conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the dirham-sized heavy impurity, identify its measure by area, and apply the conditions that affect its pardon.

Core Idea
The dirham-sized heavy impurity is pardoned for validity but not for sin—prayer is valid but makruh tahrimi.

In the Hanafi school, a certain amount of heavy impurity is excused during prayer. This lesson explains what that amount is, how it is measured, and the conditions under which the pardon applies. It also clarifies that the pardon does not eliminate the sin of neglecting removal when possible.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Ruling
The act is praying while a dirham-sized heavy impurity is present on the body or garment. The ruling is that the prayer is valid (sahih) but disliked (makruh tahrimi).
The dislike is because it is a sin to deliberately pray without removing it when possible.
2
Locate the Dalil
The proof is derived from consensus (ijma) on the fly's landing being excused and from the practice of istinja' with stones, which indicates that a dirham-sized area is the maximum that can be cleaned with a stone.
Text mentions 'because what the finger does not pick up, like the landing of a fly, is excluded from the text of purification by consensus.'
3
Trace the Wajh al-Dalalah
The analogy: just as a fly's landing is excused by consensus, the dirham amount is excused by analogy to istinja', where a stone cleans a dirham's area. The command of istinja' implies that a dirham is the maximum excused amount.
The text says 'or by the evidence of consensus upon it'.
4
Note the Ikhtilaf
There is an intra-Hanafi difference: al-Marghinani and a group hold that if the impurity spreads after affliction but before prayer, it does not prevent validity. Others hold it prevents. The majority hold the latter.
The text says 'if there was oily najis of a dirham's amount and it spread, it does not prevent according to the choice of al-Marghinani... and the choice of others is that it does prevent.'
5
Evaluate the Tarjih
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that the dirham is measured by area (width of the palm), and if it does not spread before prayer, it is excused. Prayer is valid but makruh tahrimi. If it spreads, it prevents validity.
The author sides with the area measure and notes that the majority hold prevention for spreading.

قوله (وعفى قدر الدرهم كعرض الكف من نجس مغلظ كالدم والبول والخمر وخرء الدجاج وبول ما لا يؤكل لحمه والروث والخشى لأن ما لا يأخذه الطرف كوقع الذباب مخصوص من نص التطهر اتفاقاً فيخص أيضاً قدر الدرهم بنص الاستنجاء بالحجر لأن محله قدره ولم يكن الحجر مطهراً حتى لو دخل في قليل ماء نجسه، أو بدلالة الإجماع عليه. والمعتبر وقت الإصابة فلو كان دهناً نجساً قدر درهم فانفرش فصار أكثر منه لا يمنع في اختيار المرغيناني وجماعة ومختار غيرهم المنع ؛ فلو صلى قبل اتساعه جازت وبعده أخذ الأكثرون كذا في السراج الوهاج. ولا يعتبر نفوذ المقدار إلى الوجه الآخر إذا كان الثوب واحداً لأن النجاسة حينئذ واحدة في الجانبين فلا يعتبر متعدداً بخلاف ما إذا كان ذا طاقين لتعددها يصح هذا فيمنع، وعن فرع المنع لو صلى مع درهم متنجس الوجهين لوجود الفاصل بين وجهه وهو جواهر سمكه، ولأنه مما لا ينفذ نفس ما في أحد الوجهين فيه فلم تكن النجاسة متحدة فيهما. ثم إنما يعتبر المانع مضافاً إليه، فلو جلس الصبي المتنجس الثوب والبدن في حجر المصلي وهو يستمسك أو الحمام المتنجس على رأسه جازت صلاته لأنه الذي يستعمله فلم يكن حامل النجاسة بخلاف ما لو حمل من لا يستمسك حيث يصير مضافاً إليه فلا يجوز. كذا في فتح القدير. ولو حمل ميتاً إن كان كافراً لا مطلقاً، وإن كان مسلماً لم يغسل فكذلك وإن غسل فإن استهل صحت وإلا فلا ومراده من العفو صحة الصلاة بدون إزالته لا عدم الكراهة لما في السراج الوهاج وغيره إن كانت النجاسة قدر الدرهم تكره الصلاة معها إجماعاً وإن كانت أقل وقد دخل في الصلاة نظر إن كان في الوقت سعة فالأفضل إزالتها واستقبال الصلاة وإن كانت تفوته الجماعة فإن كان يجد الماء ويجد جماعة آخرين في موضع آخر فكذلك أيضاً ليكون مؤدياً للصلاة الجائزة بيقين، وإن كان في آخر الوقت أو لا يدرك الجماعة في موضع آخر يمضي على صلاته ولا يقطعها اهـ. والظاهر فإنه قال : وقدر الدرهم لا يمنع ويكون مسيئاً أو إن كان أقل فالأفضل أن يغسلها ولا يكون مسيئاً .اهـ. وأراد بالدرهم المثقال الذي وزنه عشرون قيراطاً. وعن شمس الأئمة أنه يعتبر في كل زمان در همه والأول هو الصحيح. كذا في السراج الوهاج. وأفاد بقوله كعرض الكف أن المعتبر بسط الدرهم من حيث المساحة وهو قدر وصححه في الهداية وغيرها . أو قيل من حيث الوزن. والمصنف في كافيه . عرض الكف . هو قوله : (ومراده الخ) أي المصنف قوله : (والظاهر أن الكراهة تحريمية الخ) أقول : إن كان مراده الكراهة في قدر الدرهم فهو مسلم ولكن لا لما ذكره من التعليل بل لإطلاقه لها كما. الأغلب حيث تنصر رف إلى التحريمية، وإن كان مراده الكراهة مطلقاً أي فإن كانت أقل فممنوع بالنظر إلى الثاني بل الكراهة فيه تنزيهية لقوله فالأفضل إزالتها لأنه يقتضي أن عدم الإزالة فضيل ولا فضيلة في المكروه تحريماً، ولذا قال في النهر : هذا مسلم في الدرهم لا فيما دونه فعبارة السراج حينئذ كعبارة الخلاصة. وفي شرح المنية : إذا كانت أقل من قدر الدرهم يستحب غسلها وإن كانت قدر الدرهم يجب، وإن زاد يفرض اهـ. وذكر بعض الفضلاء عن ابن أمير حاج وفي الخانية وغيرها : إذا شرع في الصلاة فرأى في ثوبه نجاسة أقل من قدر الدرهم إن كان مقتدياً وعلم أنه لو قطع الصلاة وغسل النجاسة يدرك إمامه في الصلاة أو يدرك جماعة أخرى في موضع آخر فإنه يقطع الصلاة ويغسل الثوب لأنه قطع للإكمال، وإن كان في آخر الوقت أو لا يدرك جماعة أخرى فلا اهـ. وغير خاف أن
His statement: 'And he pardons the amount of a dirham, like the width of the palm, from heavy impurity such as blood, urine, wine, chicken droppings, urine of what is not eaten, dung, and dry dung.' Because what the finger does not pick up, like the landing of a fly, is excluded from the text of purification by consensus, so also the amount of a dirham is specified by the text of purification with a stone because its place is its amount, and the stone is not a purifier such that if it entered a little water it would make it najis, or by the evidence of consensus upon it. And the consideration is at the time of affliction. So if there was oily najis of a dirham's amount and it spread and became more than that, it does not prevent (the validity of prayer) according to the choice of al-Marghinani and a group, and the choice of others is that it does prevent. So if he prayed before its expansion, it is permissible, and after it, the majority hold [the prevention]. As in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. And penetration of the amount to the other side is not considered if the garment is single-layered because then the najasah is one in both sides, so it is not considered multiple. Contrary to if it has two layers, due to multiplicity, this is correct, and it prevents. And from the branch of prevention: if he prayed with a dirham that is najis on both sides, due to the presence of a barrier between its two sides, which is the substance of its thickness, and because the essence in one side does not penetrate into it, so the najasah is not unified in them. Then, the preventive is considered as added to him. So if an impure child (whose clothes and body are najis) sits in the lap of the praying person while he is holding himself, or an impure pigeon on his head, his prayer is permissible because he is the one using it, so he is not a carrier of najasah. Contrary to if he carries someone who does not hold himself, where it becomes added to him and thus not permissible. As in Fath al-Qadir. And if he carries a corpse: if it is a disbeliever, unconditionally not [allowed]; if it is a Muslim not washed, likewise; if washed, then if the baby took a breath (i.e., was born alive), it is valid, otherwise not. And his intent by 'pardoning' is the validity of prayer without removing it, not the absence of dislike, because in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj and others: if the najasah is the amount of a dirham, prayer with it is disliked by consensus. And if it is less, and he has entered prayer, consideration: if there is ample time, it is best to remove it and restart prayer. And if he will miss the congregation, if he finds water and finds another congregation in another place, then likewise, to perform the prayer that is certainly valid. And if at the end of time or cannot catch another congregation, he continues his prayer and does not break it. End. And it appears that the dislike is prohibitional because they permit abandoning prayer for it, and one does not abandon prayer for something dislike-de-tanzih. And in Fath al-Qadir, he equated between the dirham and less than it in dislike and abandoning prayer, and likewise in al-Nihaya and al-Muhit. And in al-Khulasa, there is an indication of difference between them, for it said: 'The amount of a dirham does not prevent and he is a wrongdoer; or if it is less, it is best to wash it and he is not a wrongdoer.' End. And by 'dirham' he means the mithqal which weighs twenty qirats. And from Shams al-A'imma that in every time its dirham is considered, and the first is correct. As in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. And he indicated by his saying 'like the width of the palm' that what is considered is the spreading of the dirham in terms of area, and it is the amount, as corrected in al-Hidaya and others. Or it is said by weight. And the author in his Kafi: 'the width of the palm' is that. His statement: (And his intent etc.) i.e., the author. His statement: (And it appears that the dislike is prohibitional etc.) I say: If he intends dislike for the amount of a dirham, it is acknowledged but not due to the reason he mentioned, rather due to the absolute usage; for most cases, when [the text is] absolute, it is turned to prohibitional. If he intends dislike absolutely, i.e., even if less, then it is prevented with respect to the second, rather the dislike is tanzihi because of his saying 'it is best to remove it', as it implies that non-removal is virtuous, and there is no virtue in a prohibitional disliked thing. Hence al-Nahr said: 'This is acknowledged for the dirham, not for less than it.' So the expression of al-Siraj is like that of al-Khulasa. And in Sharh al-Munya: 'If it is less than a dirham, it is recommended to wash it; if it is a dirham, it is obligatory; if more, it is obligatory (or even fard).' End. And some virtuous people mentioned from Ibn Amir Haj and in al-Khaniyya and others: If one starts prayer and sees in his garment najasah less than a dirham, if he is a follower and knows that if he cuts the prayer and washes the najasah he will catch up with his imam in the prayer or catch another congregation in another place, then he cuts the prayer and washes the garment because it is cutting for completion; if at the end of time or he cannot catch another congregation, then he does not cut. End. And it is not hidden that...
Source pages p. 395

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a commentary on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq regarding the excused amount of najasah in prayer. The author explains that heavy impurities (mughallaz) such as blood, urine, wine, etc., are excused if they are the size of a dirham (approximately the width of the palm). This is derived from the allowance in istinja' with stones, where a dirham-sized area is the maximum. The ruling is that such an amount does not invalidate prayer, but it is disliked (makruh) with a prohibitional dislike (tahrimi) if one intentionally prays with it. The condition is that the impurity must not spread to a larger area during prayer; if it spreads before prayer, it is not excused. Also, if the garment has two layers, the impurity must not penetrate to both sides; if it does, it counts as double the amount and is no longer excused. The text includes differences of opinion within the Hanafi school: al-Marghinani and others hold that spreading after affliction but before prayer prevents validity, while others permit if the spreading occurred after the initial contact. A key point is that the excused amount is based on area (spread) not weight. Additionally, the ruling about carrying a child or animal with impurity is discussed: if the carrier is using them (like a child sitting in lap), the impurity is not attributed to the worshipper, but if he carries something that cannot hold itself, it is attributed and prevents validity. The passage ends with a discussion on whether to break prayer if one discovers minor impurity during prayer, with guidance based on time and ability to join congregation.

Key Terms
الدرهم (al-dirham): A silver coin weighing about 20 qirat (approximately 3 grams), used as a measure of area (about the width of the palm) for excused impurity.
النجس المغلظ (al-najis al-mughallaz): Heavy impurity: blood, urine, wine, droppings of chicken whose meat is not eaten, urine of animals not eaten, dung, etc. These require full washing.
الكف (al-kaff): Palm, used to approximate the area of a dirham (the width of the palm is roughly the size of a dirham).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, how is the dirham-sized excused amount of heavy impurity measured?
A) By weight (20 qirat)
B) By area (about the width of the palm)
C) By volume (size of a chickpea)
D) By length (one finger)

Key Takeaway
The dirham-sized heavy impurity is pardoned for prayer validity but remains a sin (makruh tahrimi); it is measured by area, and conditions like spread and layers must be checked.

Praying While Carrying Impurity: Attribution Principle
Explains the ruling on praying with an impure dirham, child, pigeon, and corpse.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on praying while carrying an impure object and distinguish between attributable and non-attributable impurity.

Core Idea
Prayer is valid when impurity is not attributable to the worshipper.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq explains a key distinction in Hanafi fiqh: not every contact with impurity invalidates prayer. The ruling depends on whether the worshipper is considered a 'carrier' of the impurity. We will explore the cases of a dirham coin, a child, a pigeon, and a corpse.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling scope
Determine that the act is prayer and the ruling concerns validity when impurity is present. Note that the impurity must be attributable to the worshipper (hamil al-najasah).
2
Analyze the dirham case
Understand why a dirham impure on both sides does not count as a single impurity due to the barrier of the coin's thickness. The impurity does not transmit through the metal.
This establishes that two separate impurities do not combine into one.
3
Apply the attribution principle to a child or animal
If a child or pigeon sits on the worshipper and is steady (yastamsik), the impurity is not attributed to the worshipper. If the child is unsteady and the worshipper must carry him, the impurity becomes attributable.
Steady = independent; unsteady = requires support.
4
Distinguish corpse cases
A washed Muslim corpse is pure; prayer with it is valid. An unwashed Muslim corpse or a disbeliever's corpse is impure and invalidates prayer.
The corpse's purity depends on whether it has been washed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعن فرع المنع لو صلى مع درهم متنجس الوجهين لوجود الفاصل بين وجهه وهو جواهر سمكه، ولأنه مما لا ينفذ نفس ما في أحد الوجهين فيه فلم تكن النجاسة متحدة فيهما. ثم إنما يعتبر المانع مضافاً إليه، فلو جلس الصبي المتنجس الثوب والبدن في حجر المصلي وهو يستمسك أو الحمام المتنجس على رأسه جازت صلاته لأنه الذي يستعمله فلم يكن حامل النجاسة بخلاف ما لو حمل من لا يستمسك حيث يصير مضافاً إليه فلا يجوز. كذا في فتح القدير. ولو حمل ميتاً إن كان كافراً لا مطلقاً، وإن كان مسلماً لم يغسل فكذلك وإن غسل فإن استهل صحت وإلا فلا
And from the branch of prohibition: if he prays with a dirham impure on both sides due to the existence of a barrier between its two sides, which is the essence of its thickness, and because it is something that does not transmit what is in one side to the other, so the impurity is not unified in them. Then the preventer (impurity) is only considered attributable to him. So if an impure child in clothes and body sits in the lap of the worshipper and he is steady, or an impure pigeon on his head, his prayer is valid because he (the worshipper) is using it, so he is not a carrier of impurity. Contrary to if he carries someone who is not steady, where it becomes attributable to him and thus is not permissible. Similarly in Fath al-Qadir. And if he carries a corpse: if it is of a disbeliever, not at all; if it is of a Muslim who has not been washed, similarly; if he has been washed, then if he cried aloud (at birth), prayer is valid, otherwise not.
Source pages p. 396

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding praying while carrying an impure object. First, it addresses a dirham coin impure on both sides: due to the coin's solid thickness (the barrier), the impurity on each side does not transmit to the other, so they are not a unified impurity; thus, the ruling differs from a single impurity. Then it extends to a child or pigeon with impurity sitting on the worshipper. If the child is steady and not actively carried, the worshipper is not a 'carrier' and prayer is valid. If the worshipper carries an unsteady child, he becomes a carrier and prayer is invalid. Similarly, carrying a corpse: a washed Muslim corpse is pure, so prayer is valid; an unwashed Muslim corpse or a disbeliever's corpse is impure, so prayer is invalid. The rulings are cited from Fath al-Qadir.

Key Terms
درهم متنجس الوجهين (dirham mutanajjis al-wajhayn): A dirham coin that is impure on both sides (both faces).
حامل النجاسة (hamil al-najāsah): A person who is considered to be carrying ritual impurity on their person or clothing, which may affect the validity of prayer.
يستمسك (yastamsik): The child or animal is steady and independent in sitting, not requiring active support from the worshipper.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a worshipper carries a child who has impure clothes, when is his prayer invalid according to this passage?
A) When the child is steady and independent.
B) When the child is not steady and the worshipper must support him.
C) Always invalid.
D) Never invalid, as long as the child is Muslim.

Key Takeaway
Prayer is invalid only when the worshipper actively carries an unsteady impure being; a steady child or animal does not make him a carrier.

The Dirham Standard: Area vs Weight in Excusable Impurity
Intra-Hanafi dispute and ruling on excused impurity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi dispute on the dirham standard for excused impurity, identify the reconciliation, and apply the ruling to practical scenarios.

Core Idea
A dirham of impurity is excused, but area or weight? Hanafi reconciliation: area for thin, weight for thick.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses the standard for excused impurity in prayer. The Hanafi school has a well-known internal dispute: is the dirham measured by area (ʿarḍ al-kaff) or by weight (dirham mithqālī)? The commentator presents both narrations from Abu Hanifa and the reconciliation by al-Hindwani, which later scholars adopted. He also discusses the ruling of karahah and practical scenarios when one discovers a small impurity during prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is impurity on the garment during prayer. The ruling depends on the amount: less than a dirham is recommended to wash; a dirham size is wajib to wash; more than a dirham is fard. Additionally, a dirham's impurity is makruh tahrimi, while less is makruh tanzihi.
The excused amount (ma'fu) means prayer is valid without removal but still disliked.
2
Recognize the two narrations
Abu Hanifa has two narrations: one measures the dirham by area (spread of the coin) and the other by weight (equal to a mithqal). The hadith of 'Umar supports area, while the literal meaning of dirham as a coin supports weight.
The passage mentions 'like the width of the palm' (عرض الكف) as the area measure.
3
Understand the reconciliation
Al-Hindwani and many mashayikh reconciled the two narrations: area is used for light, liquid impurities (e.g., urine), and weight is used for thick, coagulated impurities (e.g., blood). This is the mufta bihi position.
Al-Hidaya and other core texts adopt this reconciliation.
4
Apply the ruling: karahah and obligation
A dirham's amount of any impurity is wajib to remove, and praying with it is makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked). Less than a dirham is mustahabb to remove, and praying with it is makruh tanzihi (lightly disliked).
The consensus on karahah for a dirham is cited, with disagreement on less.
5
Apply the ruling: when to cut prayer
If a person finds impurity during prayer, they must consider time and congregation. If there is ample time and they can catch another congregation, they should cut prayer and wash it. If time is short or they would miss the congregation, they may continue.
This cutting is recommended (mustahabb), not obligatory.

Source Text

And his meaning of 'pardon' is the validity of prayer without removing it, not the absence of dislike. According to al-Siraj al-Wahhaj and others, if the impurity is the size of a dirham, prayer is disliked with it by consensus; if less, and he has entered prayer, then if there is ample time, it is better to remove it and restart prayer; if it causes missing the congregation, and he can find water and another congregation elsewhere, likewise; if at the end of time or cannot find another congregation, he continues his prayer and does not cut it. And apparently the dislike is prohibitive because they permit abandoning prayer for it, and prayer is not abandoned for a lightly disliked matter. And Fath al-Qadir equated between a dirham and less in dislike and abandoning prayer, and similarly in al-Nihaya and al-Muhit. In al-Khulasa there is something that indicates a difference between them, for he said: 'A dirham's amount does not prevent and he is a wrongdoer; if less, it is better to wash it and he is not a wrongdoer.' And he benefited by his saying 'like the width of the palm' that what is considered is the spreading of the dirham in terms of area, and that is the amount, and it was corrected in al-Hidaya and others. He said: '(And apparently the dislike is prohibitive etc.)' I say: If he meant the dislike for the amount of a dirham, it is accepted but not due to the reason he mentioned, but due to its absolute application as most incline to prohibition. If he meant the dislike absolutely, i.e., even if less, then it is prevented with respect to the second; rather the dislike in it is light due to his saying 'it is better to remove it' because it implies that not removing it is a virtue, and there is no virtue in a prohibitively disliked matter. Hence al-Nahr said: 'This is accepted for a dirham, not for less than it,' so the expression of al-Siraj is like that of al-Khulasa. In Sharh al-Munya: If it is less than a dirham, washing it is recommended; if it is a dirham, it is obligatory; if more, it is fard. If he is at the end of time or cannot catch another congregation, then not. And it is not hidden that this cutting is by way of recommendation, not obligation. And by this appears what is in his statement 'and prayer is not abandoned for a lightly disliked matter,' so reflect. His statement: 'And the author in his Kafi' is in some copies, and in some it is present after his statement 'and it was corrected by the commentator al-Zayla'i.' His statement: '(And the meaning of width of the palm etc.)' said Mulla Miskin: 'The way to know it is to scoop water with the hand and then spread it, and what remains is the amount of the palm.' His statement: '(The verification of the disagreement etc.)' meaning between.
Source pages p. 396

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute and ruling concerning the quantity of impurity excused in prayer. The matn phrase 'like the width of the palm' is interpreted by the commentator as the area of a dirham when spread. There are two narrations: one for area (used for thin impurities like urine) and one for weight (used for thick impurities like blood). The reconciliation by Hindwani assigns area to light impurities and weight to heavy ones, and this is the chosen view of many mashayikh, including al-Sadr al-Shahid. The passage also addresses the ruling of dislike (karahah). Majority say a dirham's worth is makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked), and less is makruh tanzihi (lightly disliked) or even excused. The hadith of 'Umar is cited where he said 'like my fingernail' (which was the size of a mithqal dirham), supporting the area measurement. The practical ruling is that if the impurity is less than a dirham, it is best to remove it if time permits, but one may continue prayer if removal would cause missing the congregation or the time.

Key Terms
عرض الكف (ʿarḍ al-kaff): The width of the palm, used as a measure for the area of a dirham (spread out).
الدرهم المثقالي (al-dirham al-mithqālī): The dirham of weight equal to a mithqal (approx. 4.25 grams), weighing twenty qirats.
الكراهة التحريمية (al-karāhah al-taḥrīmiyyah): Prohibitive dislike; an action that is closer to haram, requiring refraining. In the context of impurity, it is recommended to cut prayer to remove it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school reconciles the dirham standard by using area for light impurities and weight for thick ones, and impurity of dirham size is wajib to remove with karahah tahrimiyah.

The Distinction Between Heavy and Light Impurities (Abu Hanifa vs Sahibayn)
Intra-Hanafi dispute on impurity classification criteria.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi criteria for classifying an impurity as heavy or light, and apply the principle of 'umum al-balwa to resolve disputes.

Core Idea
An impurity is light if texts conflict (Abu Hanifa) or scholars disagree (Sahibayn); widespread affliction also lightens the ruling.

The Hanafi school distinguishes between heavy impurities (al-ghalizah) and light impurities (al-mukhaffafah) because the excused amount differs in prayer. But how do we decide which is which? The author of Kanz al-Daqa'iq left the criterion unspecified, and a disagreement arose. This passage clarifies the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, then shows how the principle of 'umum al-balwa (widespread affliction) brings them together.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two criteria
Imam Abu Hanifa uses conflict of texts (ta'arud al-nassain): if a single text declares impurity, it is heavy; if two texts conflict, it is light. The Sahibayn use agreement/disagreement of scholars: if scholars agree on impurity, it is heavy; if they disagree, it is light.
2
Understand the role of conflicting texts
For Abu Hanifa, the presence of conflicting textual evidence weakens the certainty of impurity, making it permissible in small amounts.
This is rooted in usul al-fiqh: a text's dalala becomes zanni when contradictory evidence exists.
3
Understand the role of scholarly disagreement
For the Sahibayn, disagreement among scholars indicates ambiguity, which allows the impurity to be treated leniently.
This is based on the concept that scholastic consensus (ijma) would have settled the matter if the impurity were truly severe.
4
See how 'umum al-balwa integrates both views
Both Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn accept that if an impurity is widespread and hard to avoid, it becomes light regardless of the primary criterion. This principle is captured in the maxim: 'ما عمت بليته خفت قضيته' (That whose affliction is widespread, its ruling becomes light).
Thus the two positions often converge in practice.
5
Note the remaining practical application
The only remaining disagreement is in applying these criteria to specific substances. Ibn al-Malik notes that if a single text is weakened by ijtihad (according to the Sahibayn), that alone causes takhfeef; so ta'arud al-nassain would be even stronger grounds for takhfeef, making it agreed upon.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولم يصرح المصنف رحمه الله بما يثبت به التغليظ والتخفيف وفيه اختلاف، فعند أبي حنيفة رحمه الله التخفيف والتغليظ بتعارض النصين ،وعدمه، وقالا بالاختلاف وعدمه. كذا في المجمع وحاصله أنه إن ورد نص واحد بنجاسة شيء فهو مغلظ، وإن تعارض نصان في طهارته ونجاسته فهو مخفف عنده وعندهما إن اتفق العلماء على النجاسة فهو مغلظ، وإن اختلفوا فهو مخفف هكذا تواردت كلمتهم، وزاد في الاختيار في تفسير الغليظة عنده : ولا حرج في اجتنابه وفي تفسيرها عندهما ولا بلوى في إصابته فظهر به عنده كما يكون التخفيف بالتعارض يكون بعموم البلوى بالنسبة إلى جنس المكلفين وإن ورد نص واحد في نجاسته من غير معارض وكذا عندهما كما يكون التخفيف بالاختلاف يكون أيضاً بعموم البلوى في إصابته. وإن وقع الاتفاق على النجاسة فيقع الاتفاق على صدق القضية المشهورة المنقولة في الكافي وهي أن ما عمت بليته خفت قضيته، نعم قد يقع النزاع بينه وبينهما في وجود هذا المعنى في بعض الأعيان فيختلف الجواب بسبب ذلك ، ثم قال ابن الملك في شرح المجمع : إذا كان النص الوارد في نجاسة شيء يضعف حكمه بمخالفة الاجتهاد عندهما فيثبت به التخفيف فضعفه بما إذا ورد نص آخر يخالفه يكون بطريق أولى، فيكون حينئذ التخفيف بتعارض النصين اتفاقاً. وإنما يتحقق الاختلاف في ثبوت التخفيف.
And the author (may Allah have mercy on him) did not specify by what taghliz and takhfeef are established, and there is disagreement. According to Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him), takhfeef and taghliz are by the conflict of two texts and its absence. And they (the two disciples) said by disagreement and its absence. Likewise in al-Majma'. Its gist: if a single text declares something impure, it is heavy. If two texts conflict about its purity and impurity, it is light according to him. According to them, if scholars agree on its impurity, it is heavy; if they disagree, it is light. This is how their statements concur. And in al-Ikhtiyar, in the interpretation of the heavy according to him: 'There is no hardship in avoiding it.' And in its interpretation according to them: 'There is no widespread affliction in being struck by it.' So it becomes apparent from him that just as takhfeef is by conflict, it is also by widespread affliction with respect to the general class of obligated persons, even if a single text (without opponent) declares its impurity. And likewise according to them, just as takhfeef is by disagreement, it is also by widespread affliction in being struck by it. And if there is agreement on impurity, then there is agreement on the truth of the famous statement transmitted in al-Kafi: 'That whose affliction is widespread, its ruling becomes light.' Yes, there may occur dispute between him and them regarding the existence of this meaning in some entities, so the answer differs due to that. Then Ibn al-Malik said in Sharh al-Majma': 'If the text declaring a thing impure is weakened by opposition of ijtihad according to them, then takhfeef is established by it. So its weakening by the presence of another text that contradicts it is a fortiori. Thus, at that time, takhfeef by conflict of two texts is agreed upon. And disagreement only occurs regarding the establishment of takhfeef.'
Source pages p. 397

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute explaining the criteria for distinguishing heavy (ghaliz) and light (khafif) impurities. The author of Kanz al-Daqaiq did not specify the criterion. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the distinction is based on whether there is a conflict of texts (ta'arud al-nassain): if a single text declares something impure, it is heavy; if there are two conflicting texts (one saying pure, one impure), it is light. According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), the criterion is the agreement or disagreement of scholars: if scholars agree on its impurity, it is heavy; if they disagree, it is light. The passage then integrates the principle of 'umum al-balwa (widespread affliction): both views accept that if a type of impurity is widespread and hard to avoid, it becomes light. The commentator Ibn al-Malik notes that if a single text is weakened by opposition of ijtihad (according to the Sahibayn), that alone causes takhfeef; then if there is a contradictory text, it is even more reason for takhfeef. Thus, ta'arud al-nassain results in takhfeef by agreement. The only remaining dispute is in applying this to specific substances.

Key Terms
تعارض النصين (taʿāruḍ al-naṣṣayn): The conflict of two textual evidences (e.g., one declaring something pure, another declaring it impure).
عموم البلوى (ʿumūm al-balwā): Widespread affliction or common occurrence, making it difficult to avoid.
الغليظة (al-ghalīẓah): Heavy impurity, which requires a full dirham to affect prayer and is considered more severe.
المخففة (al-mukhaffafah): Light impurity, which is excused up to a quarter of the garment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn, an impurity is considered heavy when:
A) There is a conflict of texts.
B) Scholars disagree on its impurity.
C) Scholars agree on its impurity.
D) It is widespread.

Key Takeaway
The distinction between heavy and light impurities in the Hanafi school depends on either textual conflict (Abu Hanifa) or scholarly disagreement (Sahibayn), with 'umum al-balwa as a harmonizing principle.

Taharah — Purification

Criteria for Tathqil and Takhfif: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on impurity classification criteria.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the two Hanafi positions on what makes an impurity heavy or light, and apply the criteria to examples like donkey's water and maniy.

Core Idea
For Abu Hanifa, ta'arud al-nassain lightens; for the Sahibayn, ikhtilaf al-'ulama lightens — but both agree on 'umum al-balwa.

The Hanafi school has a detailed classification of impurities into heavy (mughalladh) and light (mukhaffaf). But how exactly is this classification determined? The author of Kanz al-Daqa'iq did not specify, leading to a subtle dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two foremost students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani. In this lesson, we will examine their respective criteria — conflicting texts versus scholarly disagreement — and see how later scholars reconciled them.

Guided Path
1
State the positions
Write down exactly what Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say about the basis for tathqil and takhfif. Use the passage: Abu Hanifa says it is ta'arud al-nassain; Sahibayn say it is ikhtilaf al-'ulama.
2
Understand the basis
Explain what ta'arud al-nassain means: two conflicting texts, one indicating purity and the other impurity. For ikhtilaf: scholars disagreeing on the impurity status. Both are ways to weaken the evidence for impurity.
Ibn al-Malik argues that if a single text is weakened by ijtihad, it is a fortiori weakened by another text, so both agree on ta'arud.
3
Analyze the reconciliation
Follow Ibn al-Malik's reasoning: The difference is only when there is no ta'arud but only scholary disagreement. In that case, Abu Hanifa would still consider it heavy; Sahibayn would consider it light.
4
Note the role of 'umum al-balwa
Both views incorporate general affliction as a factor for takhfif. The passage states that according to Abu Hanifa, takhfif occurs through 'umum al-balwa even without ta'arud, and similarly for Sahibayn despite ikhtilaf.
5
Apply to the objections
Consider the two objections: (1) Abu Hanifa did not declare donkey's leftover water impure despite ta'arud; (2) maniy is agreed to be heavy despite ikhtilaf. Explain how these objections challenge the respective criteria.
The passage notes these objections but does not fully resolve them; they show the complexity of applying the criteria.

Al-Hinduwani reconciled between the two by saying that the riwaya of measurement by area is for thin liquids like urine, and the riwaya of weight is for thick substances. Many mashayikh chose this reconciliation, and in al-Bada'i' it is the chosen view of the scholars of Transoxiana, and it was corrected by al-Zayla'i and the author of al-Mujtaba, and al-Kamal ibn al-Humam approved it in Fath al-Qadir because giving effect to both riwayas when possible is preferable, especially given the appropriateness of this distribution. It is narrated that Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) was asked about a small amount of this impurity on a garment, and he said: 'if it is like my nail' – it prevents the validity of prayer until it becomes more, and his nail was like a mithqal. This is in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. Al-Nakha'i said: They intended to say 'the size of the buttocks' but they deemed that objectionable and said 'the size of a dirham'. And by 'width of the palm' is meant what lies beyond the joints of the fingers. This is in Ghayat al-Bayan. And everyone who deviates from the zahir al-riwaya did not explicitly mention in the zahir al-riwaya whether the dirham is meant by width or weight; rather, in al-Hidayah he preferred the riwaya of width because it is explicit in the nawadir, while the riwaya of weight is not explicit but only alluded to in Kitab al-Salah where he said: 'the large mithqali dirham'. Al-Bada'i' referred to this. The author (may Allah have mercy on him) did not explicitly state what establishes tathqil and takhfif, and there is disagreement about it. According to Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him), takhfif and tathqil are based on the conflict of two texts (ta'arud al-nassain) or its absence; and the two (Sahibayn) said it is based on disagreement or its absence. This is in al-Majma'. Its summary: if there is a single text on the impurity of something, it is heavy (mughalladh); if two texts conflict on its purity and impurity, then according to him it is light (mukhaffaf). According to the two, if the scholars agree on impurity, it is heavy; if they disagree, it is light. This is the gist of their statements. In al-Ikhtiyar, regarding the interpretation of 'heavy' according to him, he added: 'there is no harm in avoiding it'; and regarding its interpretation according to the two, 'there is no calamity in being affected by it'. Thus it appears that according to him, just as takhfif occurs through ta'arud, it also occurs through 'umum al-balwa (general affliction) with respect to the class of mukallafin, even if there is a single text on its impurity without opposition. Similarly, according to the two, just as takhfif occurs through ikhtilaf, it also occurs through 'umum al-balwa in being affected by it. And if there is agreement on impurity, then there is agreement on the truth of the famous maxim transmitted in al-Kafi: 'What is widespread in affliction is light in its ruling.' Indeed, dispute may occur between him and them regarding the existence of this meaning in some specific entities, so the answer differs due to that. Then Ibn al-Malik said in Sharh al-Majma': 'If a text on the impurity of something is weakened by being contradicted by ijtihad according to the two, it establishes takhfif; then its being weakened by another text contradicting it is a fortiori, so in that case takhfif through ta'arud al-nassain is agreed upon. The difference only occurs in the establishment of takhfif.' (He said: this cutting is on the basis of recommendation, not obligation. End.) Thereby what is in his statement 'do not reject for the sake of a makruh tanzihi' becomes clear, so reflect. His statement: 'and the author in his Kafi' is found in some manuscripts, and in some it comes after his statement 'and corrected by al-Zayla'i'. His statement: 'the meaning of width of the palm' etc. – Mulla Miskin said: the way to know it is to scoop water with the hand then spread it; what remains is the amount of the palm. His statement: 'establishment of the difference' etc. – i.e., regarding the difference: according to him it is not established, according to them it is established. Ibn Amir Hajj approved it in Sharh Munyat al-Musalli; he said: here, and Allah knows best, he said in al-Kafi: 'The difference does not appear in anything other than dung and animal dung due to the established difference mentioned without the conflict of two texts; then on the basis that takhfif is established according to them through ta'arud just as through the disagreement of mujtahids, there is a need to apologize for Muhammad's statement on the purity of the urine of edible animals. Then it is not hidden that by 'disagreement of scholars' that necessitates takhfif according to them is the settled disagreement among past scholars of ijtihad before their time or those in their era, not anything more general than that. End.' Some objected to Abu Hanifa's statement regarding the leftover water of a donkey: ta'arud al-nassain exists in it, yet he did not declare impurity at all; and to their statement regarding maniy: it is heavy by agreement despite the existence of disagreement.
Source pages p. 397

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, regarding the criterion for classifying an impurity as heavy (mughalladh) or light (mukhaffaf). The dispute arises from the author of Kanz al-Daqa'iq not explicitly stating the basis for tathqil and takhfif. According to Abu Hanifa, the key is the presence or absence of conflicting textual evidence (ta'arud al-nassain). If there is a single text declaring something impure, it is heavy; if two texts conflict (one saying pure, one impure), it is light. According to the Sahibayn, the criterion is the presence or absence of scholarly disagreement (ikhtilaf al-'ulama). If scholars agree on impurity, it is heavy; if they disagree, it is light. The passage also discusses 'umum al-balwa (general affliction) as an additional factor for takhfif in both views. Ibn al-Malik argues that even according to the Sahibayn, takhfif through ta'arud is more fundamental, so the actual dispute is only about the establishment of takhfif in cases without conflicting texts. The text then clarifies that the 'disagreement' meant by the Sahibayn is the settled disagreement among past or contemporary mujtahids, not mere difference of opinion. An objection is raised: Abu Hanifa did not declare donkey's leftover water impure despite conflicting texts; and maniy is agreed to be heavy despite scholarly disagreement. The passage thus provides a nuanced treatment of the legal methodology behind impurity classifications in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
التغليظ (al-tathqil): Classifying an impurity as heavy, requiring more rigorous avoidance
التخفيف (al-takhfif): Classifying an impurity as light, with easier ruling
تعارض النصين (ta'arud al-nassain): Conflict of two textual evidences (one for purity, one for impurity)
عموم البلوى ('umum al-balwa): General affliction; a factor that relaxes rulings due to widespread difficulty

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary basis for classifying an impurity as light (mukhaffaf) according to Abu Hanifa?
A) The presence of scholarly disagreement
B) The conflict of two textual evidences (ta'arud al-nassain)
C) The impurity being thin like urine
D) The size being less than a dirham

Key Takeaway
The classification of impurities in the Hanafi school depends on a methodological choice: textual conflict (Abu Hanifa) or scholarly disagreement (Sahibayn), but both acknowledge 'umum al-balwa as a mitigating factor.

Taharah — Purification
